# Archived Note

This long-form report is retained as an appendix. See
`docs/geo_sparse_benchmarks_summary.md` for the short index and reproduction pointers.

# GeoSparse vs Dense Baselines — Benchmark Report

This document summarizes a sequence of benchmark sweeps comparing **GeoSparseNet** against dense baselines (ReLU and PSANN/ResPSANN-style) on synthetic regression tasks. It is intended to be a self-contained handoff for external review.

## Repository / Reproducibility

- Repo: `psann`
- Git HEAD: `1fe77bbb472a8f8bab3b30ba00a68d2ea35ff281`
- Working tree had local modifications at report-generation time:
  - `M scripts/benchmark_geo_sparse_vs_dense.py`
  - ` M scripts/geo_sparse_sweep.py`

## Environment

- Hardware:
  - GPU: `NVIDIA GB10` capability `[12, 1]`
  - CUDA: `13.0`, cuDNN: `91500`
- Software:
  - torch: `2.10.0a0+b558c986e8.nv25.11`
  - torch.compile available: `True`
  - TF32 enabled: `True` (matmul precision `high`)

## What Was Tested

Each sweep runs a grid over:
- Shapes: `8x8` and `16x16` (input features = 64 or 256).
- Depths: `4, 8, 12` residual blocks.
- Sparse fan-in `k`: `4, 8, 16, 32`.
- Sparse activation: `relu` and `psann` (applies to GeoSparseNet).
- Seeds: `0,1,2`.

### Models

- `geo_sparse`: `psann.nn_geo_sparse.GeoSparseNet` (geometric sparse residual blocks).
- Dense baselines evolved over time (see per-sweep notes):
  - v1/v2: `dense_relu` (plain dense MLP), plus v2 `dense_psann` (plain dense PSANN MLP).
  - v3/v4: `dense_resrelu` and `dense_respsann` (dense residual nets with RMSNorm + residual alpha; PSANN version uses PSANN activations).

### Training Setup (common defaults)

- Loss: MSE
- Optimizer: AdamW
- Epochs: 25
- Batch size: 256
- Train/test sizes: 8192 / 2048
- AMP: bfloat16 autocast
- TF32 matmul: enabled
- `torch.compile`: enabled (Inductor, default mode)

### Metrics

- `mse_test`: Mean squared error on the held-out test set (lower is better).
- `mse_train`: Mean squared error on the training set (when recorded).
- Throughput: `train_step_time_ms_mean` and `train_samples_per_sec` (when recorded).

## Task Definitions

All tasks are synthetic supervised regression on tabular inputs `X` (shape `(N, H*W)`).

### Task: `sine` (v1/v2)

Inputs: `X ~ Uniform(-2, 2)` with Gaussian noise. Target uses a few features:

`y = sin(3 x0) + 0.5 cos(2 x1) + 0.2 x2 x3 - 0.1 x4^2 + 0.05 sin(x5 x0) + noise`

### Task: `mixed` (v3)

A mixture of periodic + polynomial + piecewise terms on the first ~10 features. Inputs: `X ~ Uniform(-2, 2)` and:

`y = 0.35 sin(2 x0) + 0.25 cos(1.5 x1) + 0.25 x2 x3 - 0.10 x4^2 + 0.20 tanh(x5) + 0.15 relu(x6) + 0.10 piecewise(x7) + 0.05 x8^3 - 0.03 x9 + noise`

where `piecewise(x7) = x7^2` if `x7 > 0` else `-0.5 x7`.

### Task: `teacher_relu` (v4)

Targets are generated by a fixed randomly-initialized dense ReLU teacher MLP using **all** input features:
- `X ~ Normal(0, 1)`
- Teacher: 3-layer MLP with ReLU activations, widths derived from feature count (`hidden1 = clamp(features*4, 32..256)`, `hidden2 = clamp(features*2, 16..256)`).
- Teacher weights are sampled from a scaled normal distribution (`std ≈ 1/sqrt(fan_in)`).
- Output normalized to unit-ish scale + added noise.

## Results and Takeaways

### Sweep v1 (Sine task): GeoSparse vs Dense ReLU (MLP)

- Output directory: `reports/geo_sparse_sweep/gpu_large`
- Task: `sine`
- Command (as-run):

```bash
python3 scripts/geo_sparse_sweep.py \
  --shapes 8x8,16x16 --depths 4,8,12 --ks 4,8,16,32 \
  --activations relu,psann --seeds 0,1,2 \
  --device cuda --epochs 25 --batch-size 256 \
  --train-size 8192 --test-size 2048 \
  --amp --amp-dtype bfloat16 --tf32 --compile \
  --match-tolerance 0.01 --resume --plot \
  --out reports/geo_sparse_sweep/gpu_large
```

- Notes:
  - This was the initial large sweep using the original sine-ish synthetic task (see Task Definitions).
  - At this stage we only had a dense MLP ReLU baseline.
  - Baseline definitions and task selection flags evolved in later sweeps; the ground-truth record of what ran is the `models` and `manifest` blocks inside each run directory’s `results.json`.
  - The sweep wrapper’s CSV writer had quoting issues for list/dict fields; `summary_by_model.json` is still reliable, but `summary.csv` may be awkward to parse with standard CSV tools.

**Mean metrics by model** (computed from per-run `results.json`):

| Model | mse_test | mse_train | train_time_s | step_time_ms | samples/s |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| `dense_relu` | 0.8386 | n/a | 3.474 | 2.277 | 6.648e+04 |
| `geo_sparse` | 0.1156 | n/a | 4.862 | 3.608 | 4.656e+04 |

**Run-level winners** (lowest `mse_test` per run directory; 144 runs):

- `geo_sparse`: 144

**Best GeoSparse configurations** (mean over seeds):

- shape=[16, 16] depth=12 k=32 act=psann: mse_test≈0.01061 (n=3)
- shape=[8, 8] depth=12 k=32 act=psann: mse_test≈0.01233 (n=3)
- shape=[16, 16] depth=12 k=16 act=psann: mse_test≈0.01388 (n=3)
- shape=[16, 16] depth=8 k=16 act=psann: mse_test≈0.01405 (n=3)
- shape=[8, 8] depth=8 k=32 act=psann: mse_test≈0.01592 (n=3)

**Worst GeoSparse configurations** (mean over seeds):

- shape=[16, 16] depth=4 k=8 act=relu: mse_test≈0.413 (n=3)
- shape=[16, 16] depth=4 k=4 act=relu: mse_test≈0.3594 (n=3)
- shape=[16, 16] depth=4 k=8 act=psann: mse_test≈0.3497 (n=3)
- shape=[16, 16] depth=4 k=16 act=psann: mse_test≈0.3358 (n=3)
- shape=[16, 16] depth=4 k=32 act=psann: mse_test≈0.2721 (n=3)

**GeoSparse vs baselines (per config, averaged over seeds)**:

- vs `dense_relu`: wins=48/48 losses=0 mean(dense-geo)=0.723

**Within GeoSparse: `psann` vs `relu` (per shape/depth/k, averaged over seeds)**:

- psann better in 21/24 configs; worse in 3/24

**Parameter-match diagnostics** (models with `param_mismatch_ratio` recorded):

- mean mismatch ratio: 0.009548; max mismatch ratio: 0.03238 (count=144)

### Sweep v2 (Sine task): add Dense PSANN baseline + train MSE

- Output directory: `reports/geo_sparse_sweep/gpu_large_v2`
- Task: `sine`
- Command (as-run):

```bash
python3 scripts/geo_sparse_sweep.py \
  --shapes 8x8,16x16 --depths 4,8,12 --ks 4,8,16,32 \
  --activations relu,psann --seeds 0,1,2 \
  --device cuda --epochs 25 --batch-size 256 \
  --train-size 8192 --test-size 2048 \
  --amp --amp-dtype bfloat16 --tf32 --compile \
  --match-tolerance 0.01 --resume --plot --progress-every 1 \
  --out reports/geo_sparse_sweep/gpu_large_v2
```

- Notes:
  - Added a parameter-matched dense PSANN baseline (a plain MLP with PSANN activations).
  - Added `mse_train` and per-epoch `curve` (train/test) to each model entry in `results.json`.
  - Later sweeps changed the dense baselines to residual variants (`dense_res*`); use the `models` list inside each run’s `results.json` as the definitive record.

**Mean metrics by model** (computed from per-run `results.json`):

| Model | mse_test | mse_train | train_time_s | step_time_ms | samples/s |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| `dense_psann` | 0.9799 | 0.2217 | 5.586 | 3.493 | 4.098e+04 |
| `dense_relu` | 0.8387 | 0.1338 | 3.884 | 2.363 | 5.979e+04 |
| `geo_sparse` | 0.1171 | 0.0944 | 6.49 | 3.796 | 3.491e+04 |

**Run-level winners** (lowest `mse_test` per run directory; 144 runs):

- `geo_sparse`: 144

**Best GeoSparse configurations** (mean over seeds):

- shape=[16, 16] depth=8 k=32 act=psann: mse_test≈0.01071 (n=3)
- shape=[16, 16] depth=12 k=32 act=psann: mse_test≈0.01129 (n=3)
- shape=[16, 16] depth=12 k=16 act=psann: mse_test≈0.01219 (n=3)
- shape=[8, 8] depth=12 k=32 act=psann: mse_test≈0.01316 (n=3)
- shape=[16, 16] depth=12 k=4 act=psann: mse_test≈0.01551 (n=3)

**Worst GeoSparse configurations** (mean over seeds):

- shape=[16, 16] depth=4 k=8 act=relu: mse_test≈0.4064 (n=3)
- shape=[16, 16] depth=4 k=8 act=psann: mse_test≈0.359 (n=3)
- shape=[16, 16] depth=4 k=16 act=psann: mse_test≈0.3363 (n=3)
- shape=[16, 16] depth=4 k=4 act=relu: mse_test≈0.3282 (n=3)
- shape=[16, 16] depth=4 k=32 act=psann: mse_test≈0.273 (n=3)

**GeoSparse vs baselines (per config, averaged over seeds)**:

- vs `dense_psann`: wins=48/48 losses=0 mean(dense-geo)=0.8628
- vs `dense_relu`: wins=48/48 losses=0 mean(dense-geo)=0.7216

**Within GeoSparse: `psann` vs `relu` (per shape/depth/k, averaged over seeds)**:

- psann better in 21/24 configs; worse in 3/24

**Parameter-match diagnostics** (models with `param_mismatch_ratio` recorded):

- mean mismatch ratio: 0.009043; max mismatch ratio: 0.03238 (count=288)

### Sweep v3 (Mixed task): switch to ResPSANN-style dense baselines

- Output directory: `reports/geo_sparse_sweep/gpu_large_v3_mixed_respsann`
- Task: `mixed`
- Command (as-run):

```bash
python3 scripts/geo_sparse_sweep.py \
  --shapes 8x8,16x16 --depths 4,8,12 --ks 4,8,16,32 \
  --activations relu,psann --seeds 0,1,2 \
  --task mixed \
  --device cuda --epochs 25 --batch-size 256 \
  --train-size 8192 --test-size 2048 \
  --amp --amp-dtype bfloat16 --tf32 --compile \
  --match-tolerance 0.01 --resume --plot --progress-every 1 \
  --out reports/geo_sparse_sweep/gpu_large_v3_mixed_respsann
```

- Notes:
  - The original dense PSANN MLP baseline was hard to optimize and underperformed; we replaced it with residual baselines (`dense_resrelu`, `dense_respsann`) to better match the “ResPSANN” training style (residual blocks + normalization).
  - The task was changed from sine-heavy to a mixed function with polynomials, piecewise terms, and some trig (see Task Definitions).

**Mean metrics by model** (computed from per-run `results.json`):

| Model | mse_test | mse_train | train_time_s | step_time_ms | samples/s |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| `dense_respsann` | 0.2371 | 0.03942 | 8.3 | 6.269 | 2.847e+04 |
| `dense_resrelu` | 0.1321 | 0.02957 | 7.204 | 4.916 | 3.318e+04 |
| `geo_sparse` | 0.01682 | 0.01328 | 5.857 | 3.825 | 3.903e+04 |

**Run-level winners** (lowest `mse_test` per run directory; 144 runs):

- `geo_sparse`: 144

**Best GeoSparse configurations** (mean over seeds):

- shape=[16, 16] depth=8 k=16 act=psann: mse_test≈0.005007 (n=3)
- shape=[16, 16] depth=12 k=16 act=psann: mse_test≈0.005191 (n=3)
- shape=[16, 16] depth=12 k=32 act=psann: mse_test≈0.005205 (n=3)
- shape=[16, 16] depth=4 k=16 act=psann: mse_test≈0.005226 (n=3)
- shape=[16, 16] depth=12 k=8 act=psann: mse_test≈0.005435 (n=3)

**Worst GeoSparse configurations** (mean over seeds):

- shape=[8, 8] depth=4 k=16 act=relu: mse_test≈0.04952 (n=3)
- shape=[16, 16] depth=4 k=16 act=relu: mse_test≈0.04702 (n=3)
- shape=[16, 16] depth=4 k=8 act=relu: mse_test≈0.04583 (n=3)
- shape=[16, 16] depth=4 k=32 act=relu: mse_test≈0.03635 (n=3)
- shape=[8, 8] depth=8 k=16 act=relu: mse_test≈0.03604 (n=3)

**GeoSparse vs baselines (per config, averaged over seeds)**:

- vs `dense_respsann`: wins=48/48 losses=0 mean(dense-geo)=0.2203
- vs `dense_resrelu`: wins=48/48 losses=0 mean(dense-geo)=0.1152

**Within GeoSparse: `psann` vs `relu` (per shape/depth/k, averaged over seeds)**:

- psann better in 24/24 configs; worse in 0/24

**Parameter-match diagnostics** (models with `param_mismatch_ratio` recorded):

- mean mismatch ratio: 0.01323; max mismatch ratio: 0.0438 (count=288)

### Sweep v4 (Teacher ReLU task): remove periodic bias

- Output directory: `reports/geo_sparse_sweep/gpu_large_v4_teacher_relu_respsann`
- Task: `teacher_relu`
- Command (as-run):

```bash
python3 scripts/geo_sparse_sweep.py \
  --shapes 8x8,16x16 --depths 4,8,12 --ks 4,8,16,32 \
  --activations relu,psann --seeds 0,1,2 \
  --task teacher_relu \
  --device cuda --epochs 25 --batch-size 256 \
  --train-size 8192 --test-size 2048 \
  --amp --amp-dtype bfloat16 --tf32 --compile \
  --match-tolerance 0.01 --resume --plot --progress-every 1 \
  --out reports/geo_sparse_sweep/gpu_large_v4_teacher_relu_respsann
```

- Notes:
  - This task generates targets from a randomly initialized dense ReLU teacher MLP using *all* input features (no trig), to see if GeoSparse still helps when the target is “ReLU-like”.

**Mean metrics by model** (computed from per-run `results.json`):

| Model | mse_test | mse_train | train_time_s | step_time_ms | samples/s |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| `dense_respsann` | 0.502 | 0.145 | 7.913 | 6.499 | 2.969e+04 |
| `dense_resrelu` | 0.4419 | 0.1586 | 6.956 | 5.445 | 3.43e+04 |
| `geo_sparse` | 0.4243 | 0.3188 | 6.001 | 3.904 | 3.844e+04 |

**Run-level winners** (lowest `mse_test` per run directory; 144 runs):

- `geo_sparse`: 68
- `dense_resrelu`: 52
- `dense_respsann`: 24

**Shape-split (mean `mse_test`)**:

- `8x8`: `dense_resrelu` best (≈0.331), `geo_sparse` worse (≈0.397)
- `16x16`: `geo_sparse` best (≈0.451), `dense_resrelu` worse (≈0.553)

**Best GeoSparse configurations** (mean over seeds):

- shape=[8, 8] depth=12 k=16 act=relu: mse_test≈0.3655 (n=3)
- shape=[8, 8] depth=12 k=32 act=relu: mse_test≈0.3657 (n=3)
- shape=[8, 8] depth=8 k=32 act=relu: mse_test≈0.3691 (n=3)
- shape=[8, 8] depth=8 k=16 act=relu: mse_test≈0.3711 (n=3)
- shape=[8, 8] depth=12 k=8 act=relu: mse_test≈0.3767 (n=3)

**Worst GeoSparse configurations** (mean over seeds):

- shape=[16, 16] depth=12 k=32 act=psann: mse_test≈0.6271 (n=3)
- shape=[16, 16] depth=8 k=32 act=psann: mse_test≈0.6019 (n=3)
- shape=[16, 16] depth=4 k=32 act=psann: mse_test≈0.5208 (n=3)
- shape=[16, 16] depth=12 k=32 act=relu: mse_test≈0.4861 (n=3)
- shape=[16, 16] depth=12 k=16 act=psann: mse_test≈0.4806 (n=3)

**GeoSparse vs baselines (per config, averaged over seeds)**:

- vs `dense_respsann`: wins=23/48 losses=25 mean(dense-geo)=0.0777
- vs `dense_resrelu`: wins=22/48 losses=26 mean(dense-geo)=0.0176

**Within GeoSparse: `psann` vs `relu` (per shape/depth/k, averaged over seeds)**:

- psann better in 3/24 configs; worse in 21/24

**Parameter-match diagnostics** (models with `param_mismatch_ratio` recorded):

- mean mismatch ratio: 0.01323; max mismatch ratio: 0.0438 (count=288)

## Cross-Sweep Interpretation

- On the sine-heavy tasks (v1/v2), GeoSparse dramatically outperformed dense baselines, including a dense PSANN MLP in v2.
- On the mixed task (v3), GeoSparse strongly dominated both residual baselines; PSANN activation inside GeoSparse also consistently beat ReLU.
- On the teacher ReLU task (v4), the advantage narrowed and depended strongly on shape:
  - `8x8`: dense residual ReLU baseline was better on average.
  - `16x16`: GeoSparse was much better on average (except for a couple of `k=32, act=psann` settings).
- Within GeoSparse on teacher ReLU, ReLU activation usually beat PSANN (as expected when the target is ReLU-generated).

## Threats to Validity / Known Limitations

- **Synthetic tasks**: These are not real-world datasets; conclusions should be validated on more realistic tasks.
- **Task structure**: `sine` and `mixed` depend heavily on early features; this may interact with GeoSparse’s locality pattern.
- **Approximate param matching**: Widths are discretized; some configs have mismatch ratios above the nominal tolerance.
- **Sequential training + RNG**: In `benchmark_geo_sparse_vs_dense.py`, the three models are initialized/trained sequentially without reseeding between them; across runs this can add noise to baseline comparisons.
- **Compute/memory parity**: Equal parameter count does not guarantee equal FLOPs or memory traffic; throughput results should be interpreted separately from accuracy.

## How To Reproduce

From the repo root (`/workspace/psann` in the container, or `/home/nickm1128/psann` on host):

1. Ensure Python can import `src/` (the scripts add it automatically).
2. Run a sweep command from the sections above (v3/v4 are the most relevant).
3. Inspect outputs:
   - `summary_by_model.json`: mean metrics per model
   - `summary.csv`: per-run per-model rows (one run directory corresponds to one config+seed)
   - each run directory contains `results.json` (full details, curves)
